<p><b>North Rhine-Westphalia</b> (German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Nordrhein-Westfalen</i></span>, <small>pronounced</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ˈnɔʁtʁaɪ̯n vɛstˈfaːlən]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:De-Nordrhein-Westfalen.ogg" title="File:De-Nordrhein-Westfalen.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7a/De-Nordrhein-Westfalen.ogg" title="De-Nordrhein-Westfalen.ogg">listen</a>)</small>, commonly shortened to <b>NRW</b>) is the most populous <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, with a population of approximately 18 million, and the fourth largest by area. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>; the most populous city is <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. Four of Germany's ten largest cities—<a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Essen" title="Essen">Essen</a>—are located within the state, as well as the largest metropolitan area on the European continent, <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a>.</p>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia was formed in 1946 as a merger of the provinces of <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine" title="North Rhine">North Rhine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Westphalia" title="Province of Westphalia">Westphalia</a>, both formerly parts of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Free_State_of_Lippe" title="Free State of Lippe">Free State of Lippe</a>. The state has been <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Politics of North Rhine-Westphalia">run</a> by a coalition of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democrats</a> (SPD) and <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Greens</a> since 2010.</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="History of North Rhine-Westphalia">History of North Rhine-Westphalia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rhineland">Rhineland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Rhineland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a></div>
<p>The first written account of the area was by its conqueror, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>, the territories west of the Rhine were occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Eburones" title="Eburones">Eburones</a> and east of the Rhine he reported the <a href="/wiki/Ubii" title="Ubii">Ubii</a> (across from Cologne) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugambri" title="Sugambri">Sugambri</a> to their north. The Ubii and some other Germanic tribes such as the <a href="/wiki/Cugerni" title="Cugerni">Cugerni</a> were later settled on the west side of the Rhine in the Roman province of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a>. Julius Caesar conquered the tribes on the left bank, and Augustus established numerous fortified posts on the Rhine, but the Romans never succeeded in gaining a firm footing on the right bank, where the Sugambri neighboured several other tribes including the <a href="/wiki/Tencteri" title="Tencteri">Tencteri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Usipetes" title="Usipetes">Usipetes</a>. North of the Sigambri and the Rhine region were the <a href="/wiki/Bructeri" title="Bructeri">Bructeri</a>.</p>
<p>As the power of the Roman empire declined many of these tribes came to be seen collectively as <a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_Franks" title="Ripuarian Franks">Ripuarian Franks</a> and they pushed forward along both banks of the Rhine, and by the end of the 5th century had conquered all the lands that had formerly been under Roman influence. By the 8th century the Frankish dominion was firmly established in western Germany and northern Gaul. But at the same time, to the north, Westphalia was being taken over by <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a> pushing south.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merovingians" title="Merovingians">Merovingian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carolingians" title="Carolingians">Carolingian</a> Franks eventually built an empire which controlled first their Ripuarian kin, and then also the Saxons. On the division of the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a> the part of the province to the east of the river fell to <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a>, while that to the west remained with the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Lotharingia" title="Lotharingia">Lotharingia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eb1911_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-eb1911-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the time of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otto_I" title="Otto I">Otto I</a> (d. 973) both banks of the Rhine had become part of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, and the Rhenish territory was divided between the duchies of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Lorraine" title="Upper Lorraine">Upper Lorraine</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Moselle" title="Moselle">Moselle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lower_Lorraine" title="Lower Lorraine">Lower Lorraine</a> on the Meuse. The <a href="/wiki/Ottonian_dynasty" title="Ottonian dynasty">Ottonian dynasty</a> had both Saxon and Frankish ancestry.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia,_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4434" data-file-width="5000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia%2C_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg/220px-1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia%2C_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia%2C_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg/330px-1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia%2C_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia%2C_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg/440px-1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia%2C_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1801_Cary_Map_of_Westphalia,_Germany_-_Geographicus_-_Westphalia-cary-1799.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Rhenish%E2%80%93Westphalian_Circle" title="Lower Rhenish–Westphalian Circle">Lower Rhenish–Westphalian Circle</a> in 1799 by <a href="/wiki/John_Cary" title="John Cary">John Cary</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the central power of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> weakened, the Rhineland split into numerous small independent principalities, each with its separate vicissitudes and special chronicles. The old Lotharingian divisions became obsolete, although the name survives for example in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorraine_(region)" title="Lorraine (region)">Lorraine</a> in France, and throughout the Middle Ages and even into modern times the nobility of these areas often sought to preserve the idea of a preeminent <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">Duke</a> within Lotharingia, something claimed by the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Limburg" title="Duchy of Limburg">Dukes of Limburg</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brabant" title="Duchy of Brabant">Dukes of Brabant</a>. Such struggles as the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Limburg_Succession" title="War of the Limburg Succession">War of the Limburg Succession</a> therefore continued to create military and political links between what is now Rhineland-Westphalia, and neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.</p>
<p>In spite of its dismembered condition, and the sufferings it underwent at the hands of its French neighbours in various periods of warfare, the Rhenish territory prospered greatly and stood in the foremost rank of German culture and progress. Aachen was the place of coronation of the German emperors, and the ecclesiastical principalities of the Rhine bulked largely in German history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eb1911_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-eb1911-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prussia first set foot on the Rhine in 1609 by the occupation of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cleves" title="Duchy of Cleves">Duchy of Cleves</a> and about a century later <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Guelders" title="Prussian Guelders">Upper Guelders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moers" title="Moers">Moers</a> also became Prussian. At the peace of Basel in 1795 the whole of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_bank_of_the_Rhine" title="Left bank of the Rhine">left bank of the Rhine</a> was resigned to France, and in 1806 the Rhenish princes all joined the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a>.</p>
<p>After the Congress of Vienna, Prussia was awarded with the entire <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a>, which included the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Berg" title="Grand Duchy of Berg">Grand Duchy of Berg</a>, the ecclesiastic electorates of <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Trier" title="Electorate of Trier">Trier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Cologne" title="Electorate of Cologne">Cologne</a>, the free cities of <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, and nearly a hundred small lordships and abbeys. The Prussian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhine_province" title="Rhine province">Rhine province</a> was formed in 1822 and Prussia had the tact to leave them in undisturbed possession of the liberal institutions they had become accustomed to under the republican rule of the French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eb1911_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-eb1911-3">[3]</a></sup> In 1920, the districts of <a href="/wiki/Eupen" title="Eupen">Eupen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malmedy" title="Malmedy">Malmedy</a> were transferred to <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> (see <a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community of Belgium</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Westphalia">Westphalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Westphalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Westphalia" title="Westphalia">Westphalia</a></div>
<p>Around 1 AD there were numerous incursions through Westphalia and perhaps even some permanent <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> or Romanized settlements. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Teutoburg_Forest" title="Battle of Teutoburg Forest">Battle of Teutoburg Forest</a> took place near Osnabrück (as mentioned, it is disputed whether this is in Westphalia) and some of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_tribes" title="Germanic tribes">Germanic tribes</a> who fought at this battle came from the area of Westphalia. <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> is thought to have spent considerable time in <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">Paderborn</a> and nearby parts. His <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Wars" title="Saxon Wars">Saxon Wars</a> also partly took place in what is thought of as Westphalia today. Popular legends link his adversary <a href="/wiki/Widukind" title="Widukind">Widukind</a> to places near <a href="/wiki/Detmold" title="Detmold">Detmold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bielefeld" title="Bielefeld">Bielefeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemgo" title="Lemgo">Lemgo</a>, Osnabrück and other places in Westphalia. Widukind was buried in <a href="/wiki/Enger" title="Enger">Enger</a>, which is also a subject of a legend.</p>
<p>Along with <a href="/wiki/Eastphalia" title="Eastphalia">Eastphalia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Engern" title="Engern">Engern</a>, Westphalia (<i>Westfalahi</i>) was originally a district of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Saxony" title="Duchy of Saxony">Duchy of Saxony</a>. In 1180 Westphalia was elevated to the rank of a duchy by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick I, Holy Roman Emperor">Barbarossa</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Westphalia" title="Duchy of Westphalia">Duchy of Westphalia</a> comprised only a small area south of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lippe_River" title="Lippe River">Lippe River</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_(Gerard_Terborch_1648).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4225" data-file-width="5456" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg/220px-Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg/330px-Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg/440px-Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_%28Gerard_Terborch_1648%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westfaelischer_Friede_in_Muenster_(Gerard_Terborch_1648).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a> of 1648 in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster" title="Münster">Münster</a> by Gerard Terborch</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Parts of Westphalia came under <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussian</a> control during the 17th and 18th centuries, but most of it remained divided duchies and other feudal areas of power. The <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a> of 1648, signed in Münster and Osnabrück, ended the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>. The concept of nation-state sovereignty resulting from the treaty became known as "<a href="/wiki/Westphalian_sovereignty" title="Westphalian sovereignty">Westphalian sovereignty</a>".</p>
<p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, there is no dominant religion in Westphalia. Roman Catholicism and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> are on relatively equal footing. Lutheranism is strong in the eastern and northern parts with numerous free churches. <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster" title="Münster">Münster</a> and especially <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">Paderborn</a> are thought of as Catholic. Osnabrück is divided almost equally between Catholicism and Protestantism.</p>
<p>After the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Army" title="Prussian Army">Prussian Army</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jena-Auerstedt" title="Battle of Jena-Auerstedt">Battle of Jena-Auerstedt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaty of Tilsit</a> in 1807 made the Westphalian territories part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Westphalia" title="Kingdom of Westphalia">Kingdom of Westphalia</a> from 1807 to 1813. It was founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon</a> and was a <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">French</a> <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassal state</a>. This state only shared the name with the historical region; it contained only a relatively small part of Westphalia, consisting instead mostly of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hessian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastphalia" title="Eastphalia">Eastphalian</a> regions.</p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> received a large amount of territory in the Westphalian region and created the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Westphalia" title="Province of Westphalia">province of Westphalia</a> in 1815. The northernmost portions of the former kingdom, including the town of <a href="/wiki/Osnabr%C3%BCck" title="Osnabrück">Osnabrück</a>, had become part of the states of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hanover" title="Kingdom of Hanover">Hanover</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Oldenburg" title="Grand Duchy of Oldenburg">Oldenburg</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: North Rhine-Westphalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Creation_of_the_state">Creation of the state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Creation of the state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The state of North Rhine-Westphalia was established by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Zone_of_Occupation" title="British Zone of Occupation">British military administration</a>'s "Operation Marriage" on 23 August 1946, by merging the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Westphalia" title="Province of Westphalia">province of Westphalia</a> and the northern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine_Province" title="Rhine Province">Rhine Province</a>, both being political divisions of the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Prussia" title="State of Prussia">state of Prussia</a> within the <a href="/wiki/German_Reich" title="German Reich">German Reich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistoryNRW_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-HistoryNRW-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DWNRW_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-DWNRW-5">[5]</a></sup> On 21 January 1947, the former state of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lippe_(state)" title="Lippe (state)">Lippe</a> was merged with North Rhine-Westphalia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HistoryNRW_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-HistoryNRW-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Constitution of North Rhine-Westphalia">constitution of North Rhine-Westphalia</a> was then ratified through a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_Rhine-Westphalia_Topography_08.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2508" data-file-width="2500" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/North_Rhine-Westphalia_Topography_08.png/220px-North_Rhine-Westphalia_Topography_08.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/North_Rhine-Westphalia_Topography_08.png/330px-North_Rhine-Westphalia_Topography_08.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/North_Rhine-Westphalia_Topography_08.png/440px-North_Rhine-Westphalia_Topography_08.png 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abendsonne_%C3%BCber_Glehn.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abendsonne_%C3%BCber_Glehn.JPG/220px-Abendsonne_%C3%BCber_Glehn.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abendsonne_%C3%BCber_Glehn.JPG/330px-Abendsonne_%C3%BCber_Glehn.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abendsonne_%C3%BCber_Glehn.JPG/440px-Abendsonne_%C3%BCber_Glehn.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhein-Ruhr-Region-LEP.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="929" data-file-width="1033" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Rhein-Ruhr-Region-LEP.png/220px-Rhein-Ruhr-Region-LEP.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Rhein-Ruhr-Region-LEP.png/330px-Rhein-Ruhr-Region-LEP.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Rhein-Ruhr-Region-LEP.png/440px-Rhein-Ruhr-Region-LEP.png 2x" width="220"/></a>

<a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> metropolitan area, the largest <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a> of the European continent (population: 11 million)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia encompasses the plains of the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Rhine" title="Lower Rhine">Lower Rhine</a> region and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Uplands" title="Central Uplands">Central Uplands</a> (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Die_Mittelgebirge" title="Die Mittelgebirge">die Mittelgebirge</a></i>) up to the gorge of <a href="/wiki/Porta_Westfalica_(gorge)" title="Porta Westfalica (gorge)">Porta Westfalica</a>. The state covers an area of 34,083 km<sup>2</sup> (13,160 sq mi) and shares borders with <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> in the southwest and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> in the west and northwest. It has borders with the German states of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a> to the north and northeast, <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a> to the south and <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a> to the southeast.</p>
<p>Approximately half of the state is located in the relative low-lying terrain of the <a href="/wiki/Westphalian_Lowland" title="Westphalian Lowland">Westphalian Lowland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a>, both extending broadly into the <a href="/wiki/North_German_Plain" title="North German Plain">North German Plain</a>. A few isolated hill ranges are located within these lowlands, among them the Hohe Mark, the <a href="/wiki/Beckum_Hills" title="Beckum Hills">Beckum Hills</a>, the Baumberge and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stemmer_Berge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stemmer Berge (page does not exist)">Stemmer Berge</a>.<br/>
The terrain rises towards the south and in the east of the state into parts of Germany's <a href="/wiki/Central_Uplands" title="Central Uplands">Central Uplands</a>. These hill ranges are the <a href="/wiki/Weser_Uplands" title="Weser Uplands">Weser Uplands</a> - including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egge_Hills" title="Egge Hills">Egge Hills</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wiehen_Hills" title="Wiehen Hills">Wiehen Hills</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wesergebirge" title="Wesergebirge">Wesergebirge</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Teutoburg_Forest" title="Teutoburg Forest">Teutoburg Forest</a> in the east, the <a href="/wiki/Sauerland" title="Sauerland">Sauerland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bergisches_Land" title="Bergisches Land">Bergisches Land</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Siegerland" title="Siegerland">Siegerland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Siebengebirge" title="Siebengebirge">Siebengebirge</a> in the south, as well as the left-Rhenish <a href="/wiki/Eifel" title="Eifel">Eifel</a> in the southwest of the state. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rothaargebirge" title="Rothaargebirge">Rothaargebirge</a> in the border region with <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a> rises to height of about 800 m above sea level. The highest of these mountains are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Langenberg_(Rothaargebirge)" title="Langenberg (Rothaargebirge)">Langenberg</a>, at 843.2 m above sea level, the <a href="/wiki/Kahler_Asten" title="Kahler Asten">Kahler Asten</a> (840.7 m) and the Clemensberg (839.2 m).</p>
<p>The planimetrically-determined centre of North Rhine-Westphalia is located in the south of Dortmund-Aplerbeck in the Aplerbecker Mark (51° 28' N, 7° 33' Ö). Its westernmost point is situated near <a href="/wiki/Selfkant" title="Selfkant">Selfkant</a> close to the Dutch border, the easternmost near <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6xter" title="Höxter">Höxter</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Weser" title="Weser">Weser</a>. The southernmost point lies near <a href="/wiki/Hellenthal" title="Hellenthal">Hellenthal</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Eifel" title="Eifel">Eifel</a> region. The northernmost point is the NRW-Nordpunkt near <a href="/wiki/Rahden" title="Rahden">Rahden</a> in the northeast of the state. The Nordpunkt is located only 100 km to the south of the North Sea coast. The deepest natural dip is arranged in the district Zyfflich in the city of <a href="/wiki/Kranenburg,_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Kranenburg, North Rhine-Westphalia">Kranenburg</a> with 9.2 m above sea level in the northwest of the state. Though, the deepest point overground results from mining. The open-pit Hambach reaches at <a href="/wiki/Niederzier" title="Niederzier">Niederzier</a> a deep of 293 m below sea level. At the same time, this is the deepest man-made dip in Germany.</p>
<p>The most important rivers flowing at least partially through North Rhine-Westphalia include: the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_(river)" title="Ruhr (river)">Ruhr</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ems_(river)" title="Ems (river)">Ems</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lippe_River" title="Lippe River">Lippe</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Weser" title="Weser">Weser</a>. The Rhine is by far the most important river in North Rhine-Westphalia: it enters the state as <a href="/wiki/Middle_Rhine" title="Middle Rhine">Middle Rhine</a> near Bad Honnef, where still being part of the <a href="/wiki/Mittelrhein_(wine_region)" title="Mittelrhein (wine region)">Mittelrhein wine region</a>. It changes into the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Rhine" title="Lower Rhine">Lower Rhine</a> near Bad Godesberg and leaves North Rhine-Westphalia near Emmerich at a width of 730 metres. Almost immediately after entering the Netherlands, the Rhine splits into many branches.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pader_(river)" title="Pader (river)">Pader</a>, which flows entirely within the city of <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">Paderborn</a>, is considered Germany's shortest river.</p>
<p>For many, North Rhine-Westphalia is synonymous with industrial areas and urban agglomerations. However, the largest part of the state is used for agriculture (almost 52%) and forests (25%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="List of places in North Rhine-Westphalia">List of places in North Rhine-Westphalia</a></div>
<p>The state consists of five <a href="/wiki/Regierungsbezirk" title="Regierungsbezirk">government regions</a> (<i>Regierungsbezirke</i>), divided into 31 districts (<i><a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Germany" title="Districts of Germany">Kreise</a></i>) and 23 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_districts_of_Germany" title="Urban districts of Germany">urban districts</a> (<i>kreisfreie Städte</i>). In total, North Rhine-Westphalia has 396 municipalities (1997), including the urban districts, which are municipalities by themselves. The government regions have an assembly elected by the districts and municipalities, while the <i>Landschaftsverband have a directly elected assembly.</i></p>
<p>The five government regions of North Rhine-Westphalia each belong to one of the two <i><a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany#Area_associations_.28Landschaftsverb.C3.A4nde.29" title="States of Germany">Landschaftsverbände</a></i>:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Borders">Borders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Borders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The state's area covers a maximum distance of 291 km from north to south, and 266 km from east to west. The total length of the state's borders is 1,645 km. The following countries and states have a border with North Rhine-Westphalia:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> (99 km)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> (387 km)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a> (583 km)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a> (269 km)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a> (307 km)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg/220px-Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg/330px-Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg/440px-Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raddampfer_Goethe_bei_Nacht001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> (Köln) is the largest city of North Rhine-Westphalia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia has a population of approximately 17.5 million inhabitants (more than the entire <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_East_Germany" title="Former East Germany">former East Germany</a>, and slightly more than the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>) and is centred around the polycentric <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_regions_in_Germany" title="Metropolitan regions in Germany">metropolitan region</a>, which includes the industrial <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> region and the Rhenish cities of <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>. 30 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_with_more_than_100,000_inhabitants" title="List of cities in Germany with more than 100,000 inhabitants">80 largest cities in Germany</a> are located within North Rhine-Westphalia. The state's capital is Düsseldorf, the state's largest city is Cologne. The number of births reached 160.478 while 204.373 died in 2015. The TRF reached 1.52 (2015) and was highest in Lippe (1.72) and lowest in Bochum (1.29).</p>

<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:DarkSlateGray; width:23%; overflow: hidden;">  </div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">23%</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>According to studies of the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_University_Bochum" title="Ruhr University Bochum">Ruhr University Bochum</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> 42.24% of the North Rhine-Westphalian population adheres to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, 28.35% are members of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_in_Germany" title="Evangelical Church in Germany">Evangelical Church in Germany</a>, 23.76% are unaffiliated, non-religious or atheists, 2.78% are <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>, 0.49% are adherents of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>, 1.05% are members of smaller Christian groups (half of them the <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a>), 1.0% are adherents of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_religious_movements" title="New religious movements">new religions</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esotericism" title="Esotericism">esoteric</a> groups, 0.2% are adherents of <a href="/wiki/Indian_religions" title="Indian religions">Indian religions</a>, and 0.17% are <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>.</p>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia ranks first in population among German states for both Roman Catholics and Protestants.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Politics of North Rhine-Westphalia">Politics of North Rhine-Westphalia</a></div>
<p>The politics of North Rhine-Westphalia takes place within a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary" title="Parliamentary">parliamentary</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Representative_democratic" title="Representative democratic">representative democratic</a> republic. The two main parties, as on the federal level, the centre-right <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">Christian Democratic Union</a> and the centre-left <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party</a>. From 1966 to 2005, North Rhine-Westphalia was continuously governed by the Social Democrats or SPD-led governments.</p>
<p>The state's legislative body is the <a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Landtag of North Rhine-Westphalia">Landtag</a> ("state diet").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRWPolitcs_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRWPolitcs-13">[13]</a></sup> It may pass laws within the competency of the state, e.g. cultural matters, the education system, matters of internal security, i.e. the police, building supervision, health supervision and the media; as opposed to matters that are reserved to Federal law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRWPolitcs_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-NRWPolitcs-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia uses the same electoral system as the Federal level in Germany: "<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_member_proportional_representation" title="Mixed member proportional representation">Personalized proportional representation</a></i>". Every five years the citizens of North Rhine-Westphalia vote in a general election to elect at least 181 members of the Landtag. Only parties who win at least 5% of the votes cast may be represented in parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRWPolitcs_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-NRWPolitcs-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Landtag, the parliamentary parties and groups consisting of at least 7 members of parliament have the right to table legal proposals to the Landtag for deliberation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRWPolitcs_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-NRWPolitcs-13">[13]</a></sup> The law that are passed by the Landtag is delivered to the Minister-President, who, together with the ministers involved, is required to sign it and announce it in the Law and Ordinance Gazette.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRWPolitcs_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-NRWPolitcs-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Ministers-President">List of Ministers-President</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: List of Ministers-President">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b> with: cultural differences between for the two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landschaftsverb%C3%A4nde" title="Landschaftsverbände">Landschaftsverbände</a>+The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruhr_Area" title="Ruhr Area">Ruhr Area</a>. Bonn, Cologne, Düsseldorf and their whole lot of museums/art institutions; Düsseldorf/Neuss and Fashion. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(April 2011)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Flag of North Rhine-Westphalia">flag of North Rhine-Westphalia</a> is green-white-red with the combined coats of arms of the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a> (white line before green background, symbolizing the river Rhine), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westfalen" title="Westfalen">Westfalen</a> (the white horse) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lippe" title="Lippe">Lippe</a> (the red rose).</p>
<p>According to legend the horse in the Westphalian coat of arms is the horse that the Saxon leader <a href="/wiki/Widukind" title="Widukind">Widukind</a> rode after his baptism. Other theories attribute the horse to <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Lion" title="Henry the Lion">Henry the Lion</a>. Some connect it with the Germanic rulers <a href="/wiki/Hengist_and_Horsa" title="Hengist and Horsa">Hengist and Horsa</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture_and_building_monuments">Architecture and building monuments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Architecture and building monuments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The state is not known for its castles like other regions in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CultureNRW_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-CultureNRW-14">[14]</a></sup> However, North Rhine-Westphalia has a high concentration of museums, cultural centres, concert halls and theatres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CultureNRW_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-CultureNRW-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Synthesis_of_published_material" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag may be based upon an improper synthesis of sources. (April 2011)">improper synthesis?</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Heritage_Sites">World Heritage Sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: World Heritage Sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Europe#Germany" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Europe">List of World Heritage Sites in Europe § Germany</a></div>
<p>The state has <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral" title="Aachen Cathedral">Cathedral</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cathedral</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zeche_Zollverein" title="Zeche Zollverein">Zeche Zollverein</a> in <a href="/wiki/Essen" title="Essen">Essen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Augustusburg_and_Falkenlust_Palaces,_Br%C3%BChl" title="Augustusburg and Falkenlust Palaces, Brühl">Augustusburg Palace</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Br%C3%BChl,_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Brühl, North Rhine-Westphalia">Brühl</a> which are all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CultureNRW_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-CultureNRW-14">[14]</a></sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Drinks">Drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lsch_(beer)" title="Kölsch (beer)">Kölsch</a> is a local beer speciality brewed in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Altbier" title="Altbier">Alt</a> is a local beer speciality brewed in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Rhine_Region" title="Lower Rhine Region">Lower Rhine Region</a>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dortmunder_Export(beer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dortmunder Export(beer) (page does not exist)">Dortmunder Export</a> is a local pale lager beer speciality brewed in <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b> with: Music, Art and Cultural festivals. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(April 2011)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia hosts film festivals in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, Bonn, <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duisburg" title="Duisburg">Duisburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster" title="Münster">Münster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oberhausen" title="Oberhausen">Oberhausen</a> and <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCnen" title="Lünen">Lünen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CultureNRW_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-CultureNRW-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other large festivals include <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Carnival" title="Cologne Carnival">Rhenish carnivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruhrtriennale" title="Ruhrtriennale">Ruhrtriennale</a>.</p>
<p>Every year <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GamesCom" title="GamesCom">GamesCom</a> is hosted in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. It is the largest video game convention in Europe.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b> with: Classical and contemporary music. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(April 2011)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<ul>
<li>The composer <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a> in 1770.</li>
<li>A regional anthem is the <a href="/wiki/Lied_f%C3%BCr_NRW" title="Lied für NRW">Lied für NRW</a> (Song for NRW).</li>
<li>North Rhine-Westphalia is home to many of Germany's best-known <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speed_metal" title="Speed metal">speed metal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">thrash metal</a> bands: <a href="/wiki/Accept_(band)" title="Accept (band)">Accept</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angel_Dust_(band)" title="Angel Dust (band)">Angel Dust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blind_Guardian" title="Blind Guardian">Blind Guardian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doro_(musician)" title="Doro (musician)">Doro</a> (formerly of <a href="/wiki/Warlock_(band)" title="Warlock (band)">Warlock</a>), <a href="/wiki/Grave_Digger_(band)" title="Grave Digger (band)">Grave Digger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holy_Moses" title="Holy Moses">Holy Moses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kreator" title="Kreator">Kreator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rage_(German_band)" title="Rage (German band)">Rage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scanner_(band)" title="Scanner (band)">Scanner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sodom_(band)" title="Sodom (band)">Sodom</a>. Also, North Rhine-Westphalia is home to <a href="/wiki/Kraftwerk" title="Kraftwerk">Kraftwerk</a>, originally a Krautrock band for four years, then later a synth-pop band.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Economy of North Rhine-Westphalia">Economy of North Rhine-Westphalia</a></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p><i><b><a href="/wiki/NRW.INVEST" title="NRW.INVEST">NRW.INVEST</a></b></i></p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3181" data-file-width="2755" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg/220px-Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg/330px-Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg/440px-Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thyssen-Krupp-Quartier-Essen-Q1-2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">ThyssenKrupp</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Essen" title="Essen">Essen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1950s and 1960s, Westphalia was known as <i>Land von Kohle und Stahl</i> or the land of coal and steel. In the post-World War II recovery, the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> was one of the most important industrial regions in Europe, and contributed to the German <a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder" title="Wirtschaftswunder">Wirtschaftswunder</a>. As of the late 1960s, repeated crises led to contractions of these industrial branches. On the other hand, producing sectors, particularly in mechanical engineering and metal and iron working industry, experienced substantial growth. Despite this structural change and an economic growth which was under national average, the 2007 GDP of 529.4 billion euro (21.8 percent of the total German GDP) made the land the economically most important in Germany, as well as one of the most important economical areas in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Of Germany’s top 100 corporations, 37 are based in North Rhine-Westphalia. On a per capita base, however, North Rhine-Westphalia remains one of the weaker among the <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">Western German</a> states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> As of June 2014, the unemployment rate is 8.2%, second highest among all western German states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia attracts companies from both Germany and abroad. In 2009, the state had the most foreign direct investments (<a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">FDI</a>) anywhere in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Around 13,100 foreign companies from the most important investment countries control their German or European operations from bases in North Rhine-Westphalia.</p>
<p>In February 2014 North Rhine-Westphalia was ranked as the European Region of the Future<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> in the 2014/15 list by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FDi_Magazine" title="FDi Magazine">FDi Magazine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>There have been many changes in the state's economy in recent times. Among the many changes in the economy, employment in the creative industries is up while the mining sector is employing fewer people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CultureNRW_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-CultureNRW-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Industrial_heritage" title="Industrial heritage">Industrial heritage sites</a> are now workplaces for designers, artists and the advertising industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CultureNRW_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-CultureNRW-14">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a> region has – since the 1960s – undergone a significant structural change away from coal mining and steel industry. Many rural parts of Eastern <a href="/wiki/Westphalia" title="Westphalia">Westphalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bergisches_Land" title="Bergisches Land">Bergisches Land</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Rhine_region_(Germany)" title="Lower Rhine region (Germany)">Lower Rhine</a> ground their economy on "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hidden_Champions" title="Hidden Champions">Hidden Champions</a>" in various <a href="/wiki/Economic_sector" title="Economic sector">sectors</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protection_for_possible_nuclear_disasters">Protection for possible nuclear disasters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Protection for possible nuclear disasters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although there are no nuclear reactors located inside the state, the <a href="/wiki/Tihange_Nuclear_Power_Station" title="Tihange Nuclear Power Station">reactors in Tihange</a>, Belgium are near the German border. People in the Netherlands and Germany are concerned about their safety given the age of these reactors. Billions of iodine tablets were ordered to protect the population in case of a serious nuclear accident in Tihange. In 2015 the German government extended the availability of iodine tablets: now all pregnant women, nursing mothers, and minors in the state will be eligible. Tablets will also be available for those living less than 100 km from the Tihange reactors and younger than 45 years of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Education in North Rhine-Westphalia">Education in North Rhine-Westphalia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="740" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg/220px-1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg/330px-1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg/440px-1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1196-18-rwth-aachen-hg-von-hendrik-brixius.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RWTH_Aachen" title="RWTH Aachen">RWTH Aachen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RWTH_Aachen" title="RWTH Aachen">RWTH Aachen</a> is one of Germany's leading universities of technology and was chosen by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Forschungsgemeinschaft" title="Deutsche Forschungsgemeinschaft">DFG</a> as one of the German <a href="/wiki/German_Universities_Excellence_Initiative" title="German Universities Excellence Initiative">Universities of Excellence</a> in 2007 and again in 2012.</p>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia is home to <a href="/wiki/Category:Universities_and_colleges_in_North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="Category:Universities and colleges in North Rhine-Westphalia">14 universities and over 50 partly postgraduate colleges</a>, with a total of over 500,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Largest and oldest university is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cologne" title="University of Cologne">University of Cologne</a> <i>(Universität zu Köln)</i>, originally founded in 1388 AD, since 2012 also one of Germany's eleven Universities of Excellence.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="510" data-file-width="799" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg/220px-Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg/330px-Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg/440px-Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westfalenstadion_von_oben.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Signal_Iduna_Park" title="Signal Iduna Park">Signal Iduna Park</a>, the stadium of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" title="Fußball-Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, is the largest stadium in Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia is home to several professional football clubs including:</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer 04 Leverkusen</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1._FC_K%C3%B6ln" title="1. FC Köln">1. FC Köln</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04" title="FC Schalke 04">FC Schalke 04</a>,</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arminia_Bielefeld" title="Arminia Bielefeld">Arminia Bielefeld</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/VfL_Bochum" title="VfL Bochum">VfL Bochum</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fortuna_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Fortuna Düsseldorf">Fortuna Düsseldorf</a>,</li>
</ul>
<p>Other divisions:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/MSV_Duisburg" title="MSV Duisburg">MSV Duisburg</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alemannia_Aachen" title="Alemannia Aachen">Alemannia Aachen</a>,</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wuppertaler_SV" title="Wuppertaler SV">Wuppertaler SV</a>,</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rot-Wei%C3%9F_Essen" title="Rot-Weiß Essen">Rot-Weiß Essen</a>, and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SC_Paderborn_07" title="SC Paderborn 07">SC Paderborn 07</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Borussia Dortmund and FC Schalke 04 are the most successful teams in the state, with Dortmund winning 8 German Titles and Schalke winning 7. Borussia Mönchengladbach have won 5 titles, while 1. FC Köln have won it 3 times. <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Fortuna Düsseldorf">Fortuna Düsseldorf</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rot-Wei%C3%9F_Essen" title="Rot-Weiß Essen">Rot-Weiß Essen</a> have each been German Champions once. North Rhine-Westphalia has been a very successful footballing state having a combined total of 25 championships, fewer only than <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>.</p>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia have hosted several matches in the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> and hosted matches in the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="FIFA Women's World Cup">FIFA Women's World Cup</a>. In 1974 the matches were played at <a href="/wiki/Rheinstadion" title="Rheinstadion">Rheinstadion</a> in Düsseldorf, <a href="/wiki/Parkstadion" title="Parkstadion">Parkstadion</a> in Gelsenkirchen and <a href="/wiki/Westfalenstadion" title="Westfalenstadion">Westfalenstadion</a> in Dortmund, in 2006 they were played at <a href="/wiki/RheinEnergieStadion" title="RheinEnergieStadion">RheinEnergieStadion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arena_Auf_Schalke" title="Arena Auf Schalke">Arena Auf Schalke</a> in Gelsenkichen and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Signal_Iduna_Park" title="Signal Iduna Park">Signal Iduna Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>. <a href="/wiki/Borussia-Park" title="Borussia-Park">Borussia-Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Mönchengladbach">Mönchengladbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/BayArena" title="BayArena">BayArena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leverkusen" title="Leverkusen">Leverkusen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruhrstadion" title="Ruhrstadion">Ruhrstadion</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bochum" title="Bochum">Bochum</a> hosted matches for the 2011 FIFA Women's World Cup.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_hockey">Ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Rhine-Westphalia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ice hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>North Rhine-Westphalia is home to <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Eishockey_Liga" title="Deutsche Eishockey Liga">DEL</a> teams <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorfer_EG" title="Düsseldorfer EG">Düsseldorfer EG</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6lner_Haie" title="Kölner Haie">Kölner Haie</a> (Cologne Sharks), <a href="/wiki/Krefeld_Pinguine" title="Krefeld Pinguine">Krefeld Pinguine</a> (Krefeld Penguins) and <a href="/wiki/Iserlohn_Roosters" title="Iserlohn Roosters">Iserlohn Roosters</a>.</p>
